<div
class="header
artist_info_header
int-1
clearfix">














<h1
class="hed-1"
title="Don
Henley"
itemprop="name">Don
Henley</h1>














<div
class="header_btns">















<div
class="bookmark"
data-musicid="R1383"></div>














</div>













</div>













<div
class="int-1">














<div
class="content_right">















<div
class="artist_bio_container
clearfix">
















<div
class="artist_bio
short_bio">
















<div
class="artist_bio_inner">

















Out
of
all
of


















<a
href="/eagles"
class="hash">the
Eagles</a>,
Don
Henley
had
the
most
successful
solo
career.
After
the
group
initially
broke
up
in
1982,
Henley
released
his
first
solo
album,


















<a
href="/don-henley/i-cant-stand-still"
class="hash">I
Can't
Stand
Still</a>.
Although
it
wasn't
as
successful
as
an
Eagles
record,
the
album
performed
respectably,
launching
the
number
three
single
&quot;Dirty
Laundry&quot;
and
going
gold.


















<a
href="/don-henley/building-perfect-beast"
class="hash">Building
the
Perfect
Beast</a>
followed
two
years
later
and
established
Henley
as
a
solo
star
in
his
own
right.
Featuring
the
Top
Ten
hits
&quot;Boys
of
Summer&quot;
and
&quot;All
She
Wants
to
Do
Is
Dance,&quot;
as
well
as
the
Top
40
singles
&quot;Not
Enough
Love
in
the
World&quot;
and
&quot;Sunset
Grill,&quot;
the
album
sold
over
two
million
copies
and
stayed
on
the
charts
for
over
a
year.
Henley's
third
album,
1989's


















<a
href="/don-henley/end-of-innocence"
class="hash">The
End
of
the
Innocence</a>,
was
his
most
ambitious
record
yet,
as
well
as
his
most
commercially
successful.
The
album
sold
over
three
million
copies
and
stayed
on
the
charts
for
nearly
three
years,
launching
the
hit
singles
&quot;The
End
of
the
Innocence,&quot;
&quot;Heart
of
the
Matter,&quot;
&quot;New
York
Minute,&quot;
&quot;How
Bad
Do
You
Want
It?,&quot;
and
&quot;The
Last
Worthless
Evening.&quot;


















<br
/>

















<br
/>
Henley
reunited
with


















<a
href="/eagles"
class="hash">the
Eagles</a>
in
1994,
embarking
on
a
worldwide
tour.
The
group
released
a
live
album
culled
from
an
appearance
on
MTV
Unplugged
called


















<a
href="/eagles/hell-freezes-over-live"
class="hash">Hell
Freezes
Over</a>;
the
record
also
featured
a
handful
of
new
studio
tracks.


















<a
href="/eagles/hell-freezes-over-live"
class="hash">Hell
Freezes
Over</a>
was
a
major
success,
selling
over
five
million
copies
by
the
summer
of
1995.
However,
the
group
opted
to
take
another
hiatus
during
the
decade's
latter
half,
and
Henley
continued
working
on
his
fourth
solo
album,
finally
issued
in
mid-2000
under
the
title


















<a
href="/don-henley/inside-job"
class="hash">Inside
Job</a>.
He
then
resumed
working
with


















<a
href="/eagles"
class="hash">the
Eagles</a>,
contributing
to
the
band's
new
studio
album
(2007's
multi-platinum
effort
Long
Road
Out
of
Eden)
and
touring
heavily
in
support
of
the
project.
~
Stephen
Thomas
Erlewine,
Rovi
















</div>















</div>
















<a
href="#"
class="full_bio_link">full
bio</a>















</div>

of

telecommunication,

or

you


























provided

to


























appear

href="http://help.pandora.com/customer/portal/emails/new?email[subject]=Auto%20Renew"
